lady catherine be extremely indignant on the marriage of her nephew and as she give way to all the genuine frankness of her character in her reply to the letter which announce its arrangement she send he language so very abusive especially of elizabeth that for some time all intercourse be at an end
but at length by elizabeth s persuasion he be prevail on to overlook the offence and seek a reconciliation and after a little further resistance on the part of his aunt her resentment give way either to her affection for he or her curiosity to see how his wife conduct herself and she condescend to wait on they at pemberley in spite of that pollution which its wood have receive not merely from the presence of such a mistress but the visit of her uncle and aunt from the city
with the gardiners they be always on the most intimate term
darcy as well as elizabeth really love they and they be both ever sensible of the warm gratitude towards the person who by bring she into derbyshire have be the mean of unite they
